Finding O
your O
way O
around O
the O
Colchester O
Campus O
. O

colchester O
, O
guide O
, O
campus O
, O
maps O
, O
room O
, O
number O
, O
numbering O
, O
rooms O
, O
teaching O
, O
where O
Colchester O
Campus O
guide O
. O

Finding O
rooms O
at O
the O
University O
's O
Colchester O
Campus O
Room O
numbering O
. O

How O
to O
find O
a O
specific O
room O
on O
the O
Colchester O
Campus O
: O
. O

Always O
find O
the O
floor O
level O
first O
. O

If O
the O
number O
has O
three O
elements O
the O
room O
is O
in O
the O
Computing O
Service/Hexagon O
area O
around O
Square O
4 O
; O
an O
" O
S" O
in O
the O
number O
indicates O
that O
the O
room O
is O

. O

to O
the O
book O
which O

an O
outstanding O

to O
the O

between O

and O

. O

The O

years O
and O
Marina B-PER
Warner I-PER
, O
Eamon B-PER
Duffy I-PER
, O

of O

the O

and O
Tim B-PER

who O

were O

. O

, O

The O
most O
comprehensive O
exhibition O
of O
Surrealist O
art O
ever O
to O
be O
shown O
in O
Canada O
l O
opened O
at O
the O
Vancouver O
Art O
Gallery O
on O
May O
28 O
, O
2011 O
. O

The O
Colour O
of O
My O
Dreams O
: O
The O
Surrealist O
Revolution O
in O
Art O
features O
350 O
works O
by O
leading O
Surrealist O
artists O
, O
including O
Andrea B-PER
Breton I-PER
, O
Salvador B-PER
Dalea I-PER
, O
Max B-PER
Ernst I-PER
, O
Renea B-PER
Magritte I-PER
, O
Joan B-PER
Mirea I-PER
, O
Alberto B-PER
Giacometti I-PER
, O
Leonora B-PER
Carrington I-PER
, O
Brassa B-PER
, O
Andrea B-PER
Masson I-PER
, O
Man B-PER
Ray I-PER
, O
Edith B-PER
Rimmington I-PER
, O
Wifredo B-PER
Lam I-PER
and O
many O
others O
. O

Guest O
curated O
by O

Professor O
Dawn B-PER
Ades I-PER
, O
internationally O
renowned O
expert O
on O
Surrealist O
art O
, O
The O
Colour O
of O
My O
Dreams O
will O
be O
shown O
exclusively O
at O
the O
Vancouver O
Art O
Gallery O
. O

Works O
of O
art O
selected O
underscore O
the O
Surrealists O
radical O
sense O
of O
experimentation O
and O
the O
expansive O
range O
of O
mediums O
in O
which O
they O
worked O
, O
including O
painting O
, O
sculpture O
, O
collage O
, O
photography O
and O
film O
. O

The O
exhibition O
provides O
a O
stunning O
overview O
of O
one O
of O
most O
important O
movements O
of O
the O
20th O
century O
and O
features O
a O
number O
of O
signature O
works O
by O
more O
than O
80 O
artists O
including O
Dali B-PER
's O
Lobster O
Telephone O
, O
Ernst B-PER
's O
The O
Forest O
, O
Mir B-PER
's O
Photo O
: O
This O
is O
the O
Colour O
of O
My O
Dreams O
, O
Giacometti B-PER
's O
Spoon O
Woman O
, O
Carrington B-PER
's O
The O
House O
Opposite O
and O
Man B-PER
Ray I-PER
's O
Emak-Bakia O
, O
among O
many O
others O
. O

It O
will O
also O
reveal O
, O
for O
the O
first O
time O
, O
the O
Surrealists O
passionate O
interest O
in O
indigenous O
art O
of O
the O
Pacific O
Northwest O
and O
the O
little-known O
influence O
of O
early O
Hollywood O
cinema O
on O
the O
development O
of O
Surrealist O
film O
. O

This O

exhibition O
brings O
together O
loans O
from O
more O
than O
sixty O
of O
the O
world O
's O
foremost O

, O

, O

, O

, O

. O

by O

from O

. O

To O
celebrate O
its O
past O
, O
and O
look O
to O
the O
next O
50 O

which O

, O

and O

Oh O

a O

. O

More O
than O
200 O

More O
than O
200 O
acting O
students O
from O
the O
Loughton-based O
School O
will O

in O

Oh O
What O
a O
Lovely O
War O
is O
inspired O
by O
one O
of O
the O
most O
celebrated O
anti-war O
productions O
ever O
staged O
. O

The O
audience O
will O
be O
guided O
across O
the O
School O
's O
ten-acre O
site O
, O
moving O
from O
theatre O
to O
studio O
to O
tent O
to O
derelict O
field O
, O
experiencing O
and O
observing O
many O
of O
the O
events O
surrounding O
the O
First O
World O
War O
, O
its O
build-up O
, O
its O
songs O
, O
and O
its O
controversies O
. O

Founded O
50 O
years O
ago O
by O
Margaret B-PER
Bury I-PER
, O
a O
company O
member O
of O
Theatre O
Workshop O
( O
based O
at O
Stratford O
, O
East O
15 O
) O
East O
15 O
Acting O
School O
was O
run O
by O
actors O
from O
Theatre O
Workshop O
. O

Its O
first O
patrons O
were O
pioneering O
director O
and O
Theatre O
Workshop O
originator O
Joan B-PER
Littlewood I-PER
, O
acclaimed O
designer O
John B-PER
Bury I-PER
and O
actors O
Brian B-PER
Murphy I-PER
( O
George O
and O
Mildred O
, O
The O
Catherine O
Tate O
Show O
) O
and O
Harry B-PER
H I-PER
Corbett I-PER
( O
Steptoe O
and O
Son O
) O
. O

The O
School O
has O
consistently O
reinvented O
its O
training O
over O
the O
decades O
and O
this O
year O
has O
students O
from O
over O
30 O
different O
countries O
on O
13 O
different O
courses O
. O

In O
2000 O
the O
School O
became O
part O
of O
the O
University O
of O
Essex O
and O
in O
2007 O
it O
opened O
state-of-the-art O
teaching O
and O
theatre O
space O
at O
the O
University's O
Southend O
Campus O
. O

It O
now O
ranks O
as O
one O
of O
the O
most O
innovative O
and O
diverse* O
drama O
schools O
nationally O
and O
internationally O
. O

of O
Oh O
What O
a O
Lovely O
War O

and O
7.30pm O
on O

, O
and O
1.30pm O
and O

. O

News O
01 O
September O
2008 O
: O
Successful O
International O
Conference O
at O
the O
National O
Gallery O
. O

Over O
the O
weekend O
of O
16-17 O
November O
the O
AHRC-funded O
research O
project O
The O
Moral O
Nature O
of O
the O
Image O
in O
the O
Renaissance O
, O
originally O
led O
by O
the O
late O
Professor O
Thomas B-PER
Puttfarken I-PER
and O
taken O
over O
by O

Professor O
Jules B-PER
Lubbock I-PER
, O
reached O
its O
culmination O
with O
a O
highly O
successful O
two-day O
international O
conference O
held O
at O
the O
National O
Gallery O
, O
London O
, O
which O
was O
organised O
by O

Dr O
Kate B-PER
Dunton I-PER
and O

Dr O
Donna B-PER
Roberts I-PER
from O
Essex O
's O
Department O
of O
Art O
History O
and O
Theory O
. O

Drawing O
on O
the O
themes O
of O
the O
research O
undertaken O
in O
the O
Department O
over O
the O
last O
three O
years O
, O
the O
conference O
took O
as O
its O
starting O
point O
the O
moral O
purpose O
of O
the O
image O
. O

Based O
on O
their O
latest O
investigations O
into O
areas O
such O
as O
sight O
, O
memory O
and O
imagination O
, O
spiritual O
ways O
of O
looking O
and O
violent O
and O
erotic O
images O
, O
a O
host O
of O
leading O
scholars O
in O
the O
field O
including O
David B-PER
Freedberg I-PER
, O

Mary B-PER
Carruthers I-PER
, O

David B-PER
Summers I-PER
, O

Barbara B-PER
Stafford I-PER
, O

Gervase B-PER
Rosser I-PER
and O

Timothy B-PER
Verdon I-PER
reassessed O
both O
the O
positive O
and O
negative O
implications O
of O
looking O
at O
art O
for O
the O
Renaissance O
viewer O
. O

The O
conference O
attracted O
almost O
130 O
delegates O
from O
both O
within O
and O
outside O
the O
academic O
community O
, O
reflecting O
a O
growing O
interest O
in O
alternative O
readings O
of O
the O
Renaissance O
and O
in O
broader O
issues O
of O
viewing O
and O
responding O
to O
images O
correctly O
from O
the O
late O
medieval O
into O
the O
early O
modern O
period O
. O

Research O
Information O
. O

Research O
Interests O
. O

I O
am O
a O
Senior O
Lecturer O
and O
a O
member O
of O
the O
Language O
and O
Computation O
Group O
( O
LAC O
) O
here O
at O
Essex O
( O
most O
recent O
LAC O
event O
: O
8th O
October O
2010 O
: O
LAC O
Day O
) O
. O

My O
research O
interests O
are O
in O
natural O
language O
processing O
( O
NLP) O
, O
information O
retrieval O
( O
IR O
) O
and O
the O
implementation O
of O
such O
techniques O
in O
real O
applications O
. O

The O
intelligent O
directory O
enquiry O
assistant O
( O
YPA O
) O
project O
is O
an O
example O
where O
the O
extraction O
of O
information O
from O
partially O
structured O
data O
together O
with O
engineering O
issues O
played O
major O
roles O
in O
making O
the O
YPA O
a O
usable O
online O
system O
. O

I O
am O
developing O
techniques O
that O
allow O
the O
extraction O
of O
conceptual O
information O
from O
document O
collections O
and O
the O
utilization O
of O
such O
knowledge O
in O

a O
usable O
online O
system O
. O

I O
am O
developing O
techniques O
that O
allow O
the O
extraction O
of O
conceptual O
information O
from O
document O
collections O
and O
the O

of O
such O

in O

tasks O
. O

of O

articles O

: O

OF O

2010/11 O

terms O
. O

Autumn O
Spring O
Summer O
. O

Module O
Description O
. O

This O
module O
is O
one O
of O
two O
concerned O
with O
scientific O
and O
engineering O
foundations O
on O
which O
electronics O
is O
based O
. O

All O
electronics O
components O
are O
based O
on O
physical O
principles O
that O
relate O
voltage O
, O
current O
flow O
and O
the O
storage O
or O
loss O
of O
energy O
. O

All O
the O
theory O
we O
need O
to O
learn O
about O
how O
circuits O
behave O
is O
based O
on O
the O
fact O
that O
electric O
charge O
cannot O
be O
created O
or O
destroyed O
, O
and O
that O
the O
energy O
of O
each O
electron O
just O
depends O
on O
where O
it O
is O
, O
and O
how O
fast O
it O
is O
moving O
. O

How O
charges O
move O
in O
materials O
depends O
on O
their O
crystal O
structures O
. O

From O
basic O
ideas O
, O
the O
main O
principles O
of O
electronics O
are O
built O
up O
so O
that O
they O
can O
be O
used O
in O
the O
wider O
study O
of O
electronics O
to O
solve O
problems O
. O

Upon O
completion O
of O
this O
module, O
students O
should O
have O
gained O
an O
understanding O
of O
electronic O
principles O
that O
enables O
them O
to O
analyse O
basic O
network O
circuit O
problems O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
. O

After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

1. O
Apply O
dimensional O
analysis O
to O
electrical O
units O
and O
formulae O
. O

2. O
Find O
forces O
on O
charges O
or O
systems O
of O
charges O
in O
electric O
fields O
. O

3. O
Evaluate O
forces O
on O
current O
elements O
in O
a O
magnetic O
field O
. O

4. O
Explain O
the O
basic O
properties O
of O
conductors O
, O
insulators O
and O
semiconductors O
. O

5 O
Apply O
concepts O
such O
as O
Thvenin O
and O
Norton O
sources O
to O
resistor O
networks O
. O

6 O
Apply O
a O
systematic O
method O
such O
as O
mesh O
or O
nodal O
analysis O
. O

Syllabus O
. O

to O
vectors O
. O

of O
vectors O
; O
description O
of O
rotation O
in O

; O

products O
, O
and O

to O

. O

Vector O
products O
, O
and O
representation O
of O
torque O
. O

Kinematics O
: O
velocity O
as O
rate O
of O
change O
of O
position O
, O
acceleration O
as O
rate O
of O
change O
of O
velocity O
. O

Introduction O
to O
derivatives O
. O

Rotary O
motion O
. O

Charges O
and O
Fields O
; O

on O
static O
and O
moving O
charges O
due O
to O
electric O
and O
magnetic O
fields O
; O
Electric O
fields O

to O
charges O
; O

of O
charge O
. O

Potential O
and O
electrical O
energy O
. O

Charge O
mobility O
in O
materials O
, O
electrical O
current O
as O
collective O
charge O
motion O
. O

Concept O
of O

, O
and O

for O

Module O
is O
taught O
during O
the O
following O
terms O
. O

Autumn O
Spring O
Summer O
. O

Module O
Description O
. O

Cells O
are O
the O
basic O
functional O
units O
of O
living O
organisms O
. O

All O
of O
the O
activities O
of O
multi-cellular O
animals O
and O
plants O
depend O
ultimately O
on O
the O
actions O
of O
individual O
cells O
. O

Cells O
have O
very O
different O
structures O
in O
different O
animals O
, O
plants O
and O
micro-organisms O
; O
but O
all O
cells O
are O
complex O
systems O
of O
molecules O
capable O
of O
carrying O
out O
the O
interactions O
necessary O
for O
life O
, O
including O
energy O
transductions O
, O
synthesis O
of O
molecules O
, O
growth O
and O
duplication O
. O

Cellular O
biologists O
aim O
to O
understand O
these O
functions O
of O
cells O
in O
structural O
and O
molecular O
terms O
. O

This O
course O
provides O
an O
introduction O
to O
the O
study O
of O
cell O
biology O
. O

We O
cover O
the O
origins O
of O
life O
and O
then O
focus O
on O
the O
elementary O
principles O
of O
cell O
structure O
and O
diversity O
. O

We O
examine O
the O
eukaryotic O
cell O
cycle O
and O
formation O
of O
tissues O
from O
stem O
cells O
. O

The O
basic O
biochemical O
characteristics O
of O
the O
small O
molecules O
and O
large O
macromolecules O
that O
make O
up O
all O
cells O
are O
described O
. O

Finally O
the O
biochemical O
properties O
and O
metabolic O
reactions O
that O
are O
common O
to O
most O
eukaryotic O
cells O
are O
described O
and O
discussed O
in O
the O
context O
of O
different O
areas O
of O
biology O
. O

The O
module O
also O
examines O
the O
immune O
system O
, O
which O
can O
combat O
infectious O
agents O
and O
protect O
against O
re-infection O
, O
but O
how O
under O
some O
circumstances O
aberrations O
in O
the O
immune O
system O
can O
themselves O
lead O
to O
disease O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
: O
To O
pass O
this O
module O
students O
will O
need O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

1. O
Describe O
the O
origin O
, O
evolution O
, O
structure O
and O
organisation O
of O
simple O
molecules O
, O
macromolecules O
, O
cells O
and O
organelles O
. O

2. O
Describe O
the O
basic O
principles O
and O
regulation O
of O
energy O
transformations O
in O
the O
cell O
and O
how O
cell O
structure O
, O
function O
and O
metabolism O
are O
integrated O
and O
modulated O
. O

3. O
Describe O
the O
immune O
system O
and O
explain O
its O
importance O
in O
counteracting O
infection O
. O

4. O
Demonstrate O
competence O
in O
microscopy O
and O
spectrophotometry O
and O
present O
and O
analyse O
data O
from O
simple O
experiments O
. O

: O
SOFTWARE O
ENGINEERING O
. O

: O
2010/11 O
. O

. O

Autumn O
Spring O
Summer O
. O

Module O
Description O
. O

This O
module O
aims O
to O
equip O
students O
with O
the O
main O
principles O
of O
guiding O
the O
activities O
involved O
in O
software O
development O
throughout O
its O
lifecycle O
, O
including O
software O
requirements O
, O
object-oriented O
analysis O
and O
design O
, O
software O
validation O
and O
testing O
, O
and O
software O
maintenance O
and O
software O
evolution O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

1. O
Demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
the O
principles O
of O
software O
engineering O
. O

2. O
Demonstrate O
an O
ability O
to O
carry O
out O
software O
requirements O
specification O
, O
object-oriented O
analysis O
and O
design O
, O
and O
software O
testing O
. O

3. O
Demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
object O
orientation O
and O
relate O
object-oriented O
models O
to O
corresponding O
object-oriented O
programming O
constructs O
. O

4. O
Represent O
the O
outcome O
of O
each O
stage O
in O
the O
software O
lifecycle O
using O
standard O
modelling O
notations O
. O

5. O
Demonstrate O
a O
basic O
understanding O
of O
architectural O
styles O
and O
design O
patterns O
. O

6. O
Demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
software O
reliability O
issues O
. O

Syllabus O
. O

to O

. O

. O

. O

Module O
Description O
. O

The O
aim O
of O
this O
module O
is O
to O
build O
on O
the O
foundations O
of O
data O
and O
information O
systems O
laid O
down O
in O
the O
first O
year O
, O
learn O
how O
to O

and O
manage O
fully O
structured O
data O
repositories O
and O

and O

in O

, O

and O

. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
. O

After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

. O

to O

. O

schemas O
. O

and O

. O

CE213-5-AU B-COR
: O
ARTIFICIAL O
INTELLIGENCE O
. O

Year O
: O
2010/11 O
. O

Department O
: O
Computer O
Science O
and O
Electronic O
Engineering O
( O
School O
of O
) O
. O

Essex O
credit O
: O
15 O
. O

ECTS O
credit O
: O
7.5 O
. O

Available O
to O
year( O
s O
) O
of O
study O
: O
. O

Staff O
Supervisor O
: O
Dr O
P B-PER
Scott I-PER
. O

Teaching O
Staff O
: O
Dr O
P B-PER
Scott I-PER
. O

Contact O
details O
: O
General O
Office O
, O
email O
: O
ces-genoffice O
( O
non-Essex O
users O
should O
add O
@essex O
.ac.uk O
to O
create O
full O
e-mail O
address O
) O
, O
Telephone O
01206 O
872770 O
. O

Module O
is O
taught O
during O
the O
following O
terms O
. O

Autumn O
Spring O
Summer O
. O

Module O
Description O
. O

This O
module O
provides O
an O
introduction O
to O
three O
fundamental O
areas O
of O
artificial O
intelligence O
: O
search O
, O
knowledge O
representation O
and O
learning O
. O

These O
underpin O
all O
more O
advanced O
areas O
of O
artificial O
intelligence O
and O
are O
of O
central O
importance O
to O
related O
fields O
such O
as O
computer O
games O
and O
robotics O
. O

Within O
each O
area O
, O
a O
range O
of O
methodologies O
and O
techniques O
are O
presented O
; O
emphasis O
is O
placed O
on O
understanding O
their O
strengths O
and O
weaknesses O
and O
hence O
on O
assessing O
which O
is O
most O
suited O
to O
a O
particular O
task O
. O

The O
module O
also O
provides O
an O
introduction O
to O
the O
philosophical O
arguments O
about O
the O
possibility O
of O
a O
machine O
being O
able O
to O
think O
. O

It O
concludes O
with O
a O
brief O
overview O
of O
systems O
based O
on O
interacting O
intelligent O
agents O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
. O

After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

1. O
Explain O
and O
criticise O
the O
arguments O
that O
have O
been O
advanced O
both O
for O
and O
against O
the O
possibility O
of O
artificial O
intelligence O
. O

2. O
Explain O
and O
implement O
standard O
blind O
and O
heuristic O
search O
procedures O
, O
demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
their O
strengths O
and O
weaknesses O
and O
of O
how O
they O
may O
be O
applied O
to O
solve O
well-defined O
problems O
. O

3. O
Explain O
the O
operation O
of O
standard O
production O
system O
interpreters O
, O
and O
demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
their O
relative O
merits O
. O

4. O
Explain O
the O
operation O
of O
a O
range O
of O
established O
machine O
learning O
procedures O
and O
demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
the O
types O
of O
problems O
for O
which O
they O
are O
appropriate O
. O

5. O
Demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
the O
agent-oriented O
approach O
to O
artificial O
intelligence O
, O
and O
explain O
how O
a O
multi-agent O
system O
of O
purely O
reactive O
agents O
may O
be O
built O
using O
a O
subsumption O
architecture O
. O

Summer O
Module O
Description O
This O
module O
is O
designed O
to O
develop O
a O
range O
of O
professional O
skills O
of O
students O
using O
a O
team O
project O
as O
the O
vehicle O
. O

Each O
team O
of O
students O
will O
work O
on O
a O
project O
of O
their O
choice O
given O
a O
set O
of O
attributes O
that O
the O
project O
must O
contain O
. O

The O
projects O
are O
research O
based O
and O
incorporate O
the O
concepts O
of O
specifications O
, O
design O
, O
and O
implementation O
. O

Within O
the O
project O
students O
will O
be O
learn O
about O
sustainability O
, O
project O
and O
time O
management O
, O
design O
, O
legal O
issues O
, O
health O
and O
safety O
, O
data O
analysis O
and O
presentation O
, O
team O
reporting O
, O
and O
self O
evaluation O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
. O

After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O

Module O
Description O
. O

The O
aim O
of O
this O
module O
is O
to O
introduce O
some O
of O
the O
mathematical O
ideas O
essential O
to O
electronic O
engineering O
. O

The O
course O
will O
be O
illuminated O
by O
practical O
laboratory O
sessions O
and O
an O
assignment O
in O
MATLAB O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

1. O
Recognise O
, O
and O
perform O
routine O
calculations O
with O
a O
number O
of O
special O
functions O
, O
including O
trigonometric O
, O
logarithmic O
and O
exponential O
functions O
. O

2. O
Define O
and O
explain O
the O
operations O
of O
differentiation O
and O
integration O
, O
and O
use O
appropriate O
rules O
to O
find O
derivatives O
and O
integrals O
. O

3. O
Execute O
basic O
operations O
with O
complex O
numbers O
( O
+ O
, O
-, O
x O
, O
/ O
, O
*) O
, O
and O
convert O
between O
Cartesian O
and O
polar O
forms O
. O

Find O
roots O
of O
polynomials O
( O
real O
and O
complex O
) O
. O

4. O
Execute O
basic O
operations O
with O
vectors O
and O
matrices O
( O
+ O
, O
-, O
x O
, O
inverse O
) O
, O
and O
solve O
systems O
of O
linear O
equations O
via O
matrices O
. O

5. O
Find O
the O
Fourier O
series O
of O
a O
given O
periodic O
function O
, O
and O
explain O
the O
concept O
of O
the O
spectrum O
of O
a O
periodic O
function O
. O

Module O
Description O
. O

The O
aim O
of O
this O
module O
is O
to O
provide O
an O
introduction O
to O
the O
fundamental O
of O
object-oriented O
programming O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

1. O
Demonstrate O
an O
understanding O
of O
the O
basic O
principles O
and O
concepts O
that O
underlie O
the O
object-oriented O
programming O
model O
. O

2. O
Write O
programs O
that O
define O
classes O
and O
use O
objects O
of O
those O
classes O
. O

3. O
Write O
programs O
that O
use O
parts O
of O
a O
platform O
API O
to O
perform O
file-based O
I/O O
, O
and O
simple O
graphical O
components O
. O

4. O
Design O
, O
write O
, O
and O
analyse O
programs O
that O
utilise O
inheritance O
and O
polymorphism O
. O

Syllabus O
. O

to O

. O

and O

of O

, O

and O

. O

. O

Summer O

Module O
Description O
. O

Learning O
Outcomes O
. O

The O
aim O
of O
this O
module O
is O
to O
provide O
an O
introduction O
to O
data O
modelling O
and O
the O
design O
and O
implementation O
of O
relational O
databases O
. O

After O
completing O
this O
module O
, O
students O
will O
be O
expected O
to O
be O
able O
to O
: O
. O

1. O
Use O
examples O
to O
explain O
the O
basic O
terminology O
of O
, O
and O
perform O
the O
operation O
associated O
with O
, O
sets O
, O
relations O
and O
functions O
. O

2. O
Prepare O
a O
relational O
schema O
from O
a O
conceptual O
model O
developed O
using O
the O
entity-relationship O
model O
. O

3. O
Demonstrate O
queries O
in O
the O
relational O
algebra O
. O

4. O
Employ O
the O
notion O
of O
normal O
forms O
in O
a O
relational O
database O
design O
. O

5. O
Create O
a O
relational O
database O
schema O
in O
SQL O
that O
incorporates O
key O
, O
entity O
integrity O
, O
and O
referential O
integrity O
constraints O
. O

6. O
Demonstrate O
data O
definition O
in O
SQL O
and O
retrieve O
information O
from O
a O
database O
using O
the O
SQL O
SELECT O
statement O
. O

7. O
Use O
a O
relational O
database O
management O
system O
to O
build O
a O
database O
. O

the O
Autumn O
term O
module O
, O

Systems O

, O
CE161 O
. O

examine O
how O
data O
are O
represented O
within O
digital O
systems O
, O

point O
, O
'text O
' O
and O

' O
files O

and O
how O
the O

between O
internal O
and O

forms O
are O
performed O
. O

The O
applications O
and O
design O
, O
both O
manual O
and O
with O
CAD O
systems O
, O
of O
higher-level O
logic O
elements O
such O
as O
counters O
, O
registers O
and O
multiplexers O
are O
discussed O
. O

Transmission O
of O
digital O
data O
between O
systems O
is O
introduced O
by O
examination O
of O
the O
RS232 O
protocol O
. O

designed O
